<p><b>Hugo Hadrien Dominique Lloris</b> (<small>French pronunciation: ​</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[yɡo joʁis]</a></span>; born 26 December 1986) is a French professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">goalkeeper</a> and is the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> of both <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> and the <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> He is a three-time winner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Professional_Footballers" title="National Union of Professional Footballers">National Union of Professional Footballers</a> (UNFP) <a href="/wiki/Troph%C3%A9es_UNFP_du_football#Goalkeeper_of_the_Year" title="Trophées UNFP du football">Ligue 1 Goalkeeper of the Year</a> award.
</p><p>Lloris began his career with hometown club <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">OGC Nice</a>, made his debut as a teenager in October 2005 and started in goal during the team's run to the <a href="/wiki/2006_Coupe_de_la_Ligue_Final" title="2006 Coupe de la Ligue Final">2006 Coupe de la Ligue Final</a>. After excelling at the club for three seasons, Lloris moved to seven-time <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Olympique Lyonnais</a>, amid interest from several other clubs, notably <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>. Lloris won several domestic awards in his first season with Lyon and, in his second season, earned award nominations at European level for his performances in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>, which saw Lyon reach the semi-finals for the first time. He joined Tottenham in 2012, and helped the team reach the Champions League final in 2019.
</p><p>Lloris is a <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">French international</a> having represented his nation at <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-18_football_team" title="France national under-18 football team">under-18</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-19_football_team" title="France national under-19 football team">under-19</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-21_football_team" title="France national under-21 football team">under-21</a> level. Prior to playing at senior level, he played on the under-19 team that won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2005_European_Under-19_Football_Championship" title="2005 European Under-19 Football Championship">2005 European Under-19 Football Championship</a>. Lloris made his senior international debut in November 2008 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" title="Exhibition match">friendly</a> against <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a>. He helped France qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> and was applauded by the media for his performance over two legs against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Second_Round" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Second Round">qualifying playoffs</a>. He captained the national team for the first time in 2010, and became first-choice captain on 28 February 2012, leading France into the quarter-finals of both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2012" title="Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, runners-up at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2016" title="Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a>, and winners at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lloris was born on 26 December 1986 in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">Mediterranean</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> to an upper-class family. His mother was a lawyer and his father is a <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo" title="Monte Carlo">Monte Carlo</a>-based banker of  <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spanish</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pays_Catalan" title="Pays Catalan">Catalan</a>) descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugo_lloris_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-hugo_lloris-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> He has a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Gautier_Lloris" title="Gautier Lloris">Gautier</a>, who currently plays as a <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">central defender</a> for his older brother's former club <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">OGC Nice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>  As a youth, like his international and club teammate <a href="/wiki/Yoann_Gourcuff" title="Yoann Gourcuff">Yoann Gourcuff</a>, Lloris excelled at tennis and played the sport up until the age of 13. He was among the top players in his age group, ranking high in the country's national standings before opting to focus on football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hugo_lloris_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-hugo_lloris-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloris studied at the Lycée Thierry Maulnier in Nice until 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lloris started playing football at the age of six at CEDAC (Centre de Diffusion et d'Action Culturelle), a local <a href="/wiki/Cultural_center" title="Cultural center">cultural center</a> based in the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Cimiez" title="Cimiez">Cimiez</a>, Nice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deux_garçons_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-deux_garçons-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The centre offered a variety of activities, which included football. Lloris played a variety of positions at the centre, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" title="Striker (association football)">in the attack</a>, before switching to the goalkeeper position after coaches noticed that he possessed impressive goalkeeping qualities, such as ball-handling and catching skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deux_garçons_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-deux_garçons-11">[11]</a></sup> Lloris excelled at the position and caught the attention of former <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">OGC Nice</a> <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">goalkeeper</a> and French international <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Baratelli" title="Dominique Baratelli">Dominique Baratelli</a>, who recommended that the player join his former club. At the age of ten, Lloris joined Nice's youth academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deux_garçons_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-deux_garçons-11">[11]</a></sup> He spent several years in the club's youth academy and was the starting goalkeeper for the club's under-17 team that won the 2003–04 edition of the <i>Championnat Nationaux des 18 ans</i>, a country-wide domestic league competition for players under the age of 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nice">Nice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Nice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:165px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="228" data-file-width="163" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Hugo_Lloris.JPG" width="163"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris in 2005 with <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">Nice</a></div></div></div>
<p>After success with the club's under-18 team, Lloris was promoted to the club's reserve team in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Championnat_de_France_amateur" title="Championnat de France amateur">Championnat de France amateur</a>, the fourth level of French football, for the 2004–05 season. He alternated the starting goalkeeper spot with Hilaire Munoz as he appeared in 12 matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Lloris was promoted to the first team squad ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Ligue_1" title="2005–06 Ligue 1">2005–06 season</a> and assigned the number 1 shirt. He was designated by manager <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Antonetti" title="Frédéric Antonetti">Frédéric Antonetti</a> as the team's starting goalkeeper for the club's <a href="/wiki/Coupe_de_la_Ligue" title="Coupe de la Ligue">Coupe de la Ligue</a> campaign ahead of fan-favourite (and fellow Nice native) <a href="/wiki/Damien_Gregorini" title="Damien Gregorini">Damien Gregorini</a>, who was relied more upon in league play. Lloris made his professional debut on 25 October 2005, at the age of 18, recording a clean sheet in Nice's 2–0 Coupe de la Ligue win over <a href="/wiki/LB_Ch%C3%A2teauroux" title="LB Châteauroux">Châteauroux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> He recorded another clean sheet the following round against <a href="/wiki/CS_Sedan_Ardennes" title="CS Sedan Ardennes">Sedan</a> and helped Nice upset favorites <a href="/wiki/FC_Girondins_de_Bordeaux" title="FC Girondins de Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derby_de_la_C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Derby de la Côte d'Azur">Derby de la Côte d'Azur</a> rivals <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">Monaco</a> in the quarter-finals and semi-finals respectively, meaning the club had reached its first-ever Coupe de la Ligue final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coupe_de_la_Ligue_Final_2006" title="Coupe de la Ligue Final 2006">the final</a>, Lloris played the entire match in the club's 2–1 defeat against <a href="/wiki/AS_Nancy" title="AS Nancy">Nancy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloris made his league debut on 18 March 2006 against Nancy picking up a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clean_sheet" title="Clean sheet">clean sheet</a> in a 1–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> He made four more league appearances that season. The <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Ligue_1" title="2006–07 Ligue 1">following season</a>, Lloris was given the starting job permanently ahead of Gregorini, who subsequently departed the club for Nancy. Lloris appeared in all but one league match recording 13 clean sheets as Nice finished in 16th place. Despite the disappointing finish, the club was the fifth-best defensive team in the league with Lloris conceding only 36 goals. Only veterans <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%A9gory_Coupet" title="Grégory Coupet">Grégory Coupet</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9dric_Carrasso" title="Cédric Carrasso">Cédric Carrasso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulrich_Ram%C3%A9" title="Ulrich Ramé">Ulrich Ramé</a> conceded fewer. For the early part of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Ligue_1" title="2007–08 Ligue 1">2007–08 season</a>, Lloris endured a recurring ligament injury in his left knee, which forced him to miss three weeks in September. He returned to the team on 6 October 2007 in a league match against <a href="/wiki/Le_Mans_FC" title="Le Mans FC">Le Mans</a>, but was substituted out after 71 minutes after the injury relapsed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Lloris missed a further six weeks before returning on 24 November in the team's 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> He appeared consistently with the team for the rest of the season as Nice finished in 8th place, the club's best finish in the league since finishing 6th in the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_French_Division_1" title="1988–89 French Division 1">1988–89 season</a>. Lloris conceded only 24 goals in his 30 appearances recording 13 clean sheets. He contributed to a defense that only conceded 30 overall during the season, tied for the league-best. Lloris' efforts that season led to him being approached by several big European clubs with hopes of signing him for the future.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyon">Lyon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lyon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After another solid season with Nice, speculation arose as to where Lloris would play the following season. He was primarily linked to French club <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a>, who wanted him to replace the departing Grégory Coupet, <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>, who wanted him to replace the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Dida_(footballer,_born_1973)" title="Dida (footballer, born 1973)">Dida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, who wanted Lloris to replace <a href="/wiki/Paul_Robinson_(footballer,_born_1979)" title="Paul Robinson (footballer, born 1979)">Paul Robinson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> After reportedly coming to personal terms with Milan, Lloris snubbed the Italian club for seven-time <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> champions Lyon. Milan vice president <a href="/wiki/Adriano_Galliani" title="Adriano Galliani">Adriano Galliani</a> later declared that an agreement had been all but reached stating that Lloris was "practically ours", but the deal reached a stumbling block when Milan goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Christian_Abbiati" title="Christian Abbiati">Christian Abbiati</a> refused a move to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Citt%C3%A0_di_Palermo" title="U.S. Città di Palermo">Palermo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Lloris explained his decision citing Lyon's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European</a> ambitions, more playing time at Lyon, and in Milan, he was not guaranteed the starting goalkeeper spot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The transfer fee was initially undisclosed, but was later discovered to be priced at €8.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> He was promptly handed the number 1 shirt and also the starting goalkeeper position.
</p>
<h4><span id="2008.E2.80.9309_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–09_season">2008–09 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2008–09 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Lloris made his club debut in the team's opening league match of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Ligue_1" title="2008–09 Ligue 1">2008–09 season</a> on 10 August 2008 against <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_FC" title="Toulouse FC">Toulouse</a>. Lyon won the match 3–0 win giving the goalkeeper his first career clean sheet with the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyon_v._Toulouse_Match_Report_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lyon_v._Toulouse_Match_Report-32">[32]</a></sup> In the following three matches, Lloris earned clean sheets against <a href="/wiki/FC_Lorient" title="FC Lorient">Lorient</a> and regional rivals <a href="/wiki/Grenoble_Foot_38" title="Grenoble Foot 38">Grenoble</a> and <a href="/wiki/AS_Saint-%C3%89tienne" title="AS Saint-Étienne">Saint-Étienne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lyon_v._Toulouse_Match_Report_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lyon_v._Toulouse_Match_Report-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Despite Lyon losing out on the title for the first time in seven years, he finished the campaign conceding only 27 goals in the league and recording 16 clean sheets; both of which were second-best to only Cédric Carrasso. Lloris was, subsequently, named the league's <a href="/wiki/Troph%C3%A9es_UNFP_du_football#Goalkeeper_of_the_Year" title="Trophées UNFP du football">top goalkeeper</a> and also named to the <a href="/wiki/Troph%C3%A9es_UNFP_du_football#2009" title="Trophées UNFP du football">Team of the Year</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="715" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg/160px-Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg/240px-Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg/320px-Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris signing autographs in 2010</div></div></div>
<h4><span id="2009.E2.80.9310_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–10_season">2009–10 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2009–10 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Ligue_1" title="2009–10 Ligue 1">2009–10 season</a>, Lloris remained the club's first-choice goalkeeper and opened the new campaign by recording four clean sheets in the club's first eight matches. For his performances in the month of September, he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/UNFP_Player_of_the_Month" title="UNFP Player of the Month">UNFP Player of the Month</a> becoming the first goalkeeper since <a href="/wiki/Steve_Mandanda" title="Steve Mandanda">Steve Mandanda</a> in August 2008 to receive the award. Lloris earned media praise for his performances against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. In the first match, played at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>, Lloris made four saves holding Liverpool to only one goal. Lyon won the match 2–1. In the second match at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stade_Gerland" title="Stade Gerland">Stade Gerland</a>, he produced stops from shots by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Kuyt" title="Dirk Kuyt">Dirk Kuyt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Voronin" title="Andriy Voronin">Andriy Voronin</a> in the first half, then displayed reflexes to deny the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Leiva" title="Lucas Leiva">Lucas</a> midway through the second period. Though Lyon conceded late, the team drew the match 1–1 with a goal from <a href="/wiki/Lisandro_L%C3%B3pez" title="Lisandro López">Lisandro López</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injury_time" title="Injury time">injury time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 November 2009, Lloris, alongside Marseille and France's number two goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Steve_Mandanda" title="Steve Mandanda">Steve Mandanda</a>, each conceded five goals in a <a href="/wiki/Choc_des_Olympiques#Notable_matches" title="Choc des Olympiques">thrilling 5–5 draw</a> between Lyon and Marseille, though most of the goals conceded were attributed to "slack defending" displayed by both clubs as described by the media and both managers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-38">[38]</a></sup> On 20 December, Lloris finished third behind <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoann_Gourcuff" title="Yoann Gourcuff">Yoann Gourcuff</a> in voting for the <i><a href="/wiki/France_Football" title="France Football">France Football</a></i> 2009 <a href="/wiki/France_Football#French_player_of_the_year" title="France Football">French Player of the Year</a> award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloris remained consistent during the 2010 portion of the season conceding only two goals in the club's first four matches of the year with Lyon winning all of them and Lloris picking up two clean sheets. On 16 February, Lloris earned a clean sheet in Lyon's first leg of its <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> knockout round match against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>. Lloris made two saves in the team's 1–0 victory making a finger-tipping save from a deflected <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> shot in the 61st minute and producing a reflex save on a shot from <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Higua%C3%ADn" title="Gonzalo Higuaín">Gonzalo Higuaín</a> three minutes later to keep Lyon ahead on the scoreline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Lyon later achieved qualification to the quarterfinals in the competition after drawing 1–1 in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> with Lloris conceding the opening goal to Cristiano Ronaldo in the sixth minute. It was the goalkeeper's first goal conceded in over 620 minutes. On 2 May, Lloris provided the assist on the game-winning goal scored by <a href="/wiki/Michel_Bastos" title="Michel Bastos">Michel Bastos</a> in Lyon's 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Montpellier_HSC" title="Montpellier HSC">Montpellier</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> A week later, he was named, for the second consecutive season, the UNFP Ligue 1 Goalkeeper of the Year.
</p>
<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.9311_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–11_season">2010–11 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010–11 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Ligue_1" title="2010–11 Ligue 1">2010–11 season</a>, Lloris was nominated for the UEFA Club Goalkeeper of the Year award at the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Club_Football_Awards" title="UEFA Club Football Awards">UEFA Club Football Awards</a>, but lost out on the award to <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2010 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League</a>-winning keeper <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_C%C3%A9sar_(football_goalkeeper,_born_1979)" title="Júlio César (football goalkeeper, born 1979)">Júlio César</a> of <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In the season, Lloris performed well, despite conceding a career-high 40 goals in the league as Lyon failed to win the league for the third consecutive season. The frustrating season for the club and Lloris himself reached its zenith on 3 April 2011 following the club's 2–2 away draw with Lloris' former club Nice. Despite being up 2–0 heading into injury time, Lyon conceded two goals within two minutes of each other, an <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Mouloungui" title="Éric Mouloungui">Éric Mouloungui</a> penalty and a goal at the death from <a href="/wiki/Renato_Civelli" title="Renato Civelli">Renato Civelli</a>, allowing Nice to leave the match with a draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Following the conclusion of the match, a disappointed Lloris, who had previously saved a penalty shot in the match, delivered a surprising profanity-laced declaration in the team's locker room, in which he questioned the team's overall performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Following the team's 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/RC_Lens" title="RC Lens">Lens</a> the following week, in which Lloris earned his first clean sheet in over a month, the goalkeeper reflected on his comments after the Nice match, stating, "It was a human reaction. There was frustration and accumulation and it had to come out. It was intolerable to draw 2–2 when leading 2–0."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tottenham_Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tottenham Hotspur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_(15929521516).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2019" data-file-width="3028" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg/220px-LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg/330px-LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg/440px-LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_%2815929521516%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LlorisChelsea_3_Spurs_0_(15929521516).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris making a save for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9313_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–13_season">2012–13 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2012–13 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Lloris signed for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> on 31 August 2012 for €10 million and €5 million variable. Lyon also receives 20% of Lloris's future transfer profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He made his debut for Spurs in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a> on 20 September 2012, the result of the match was 0–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Lloris started his first <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> game against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> on 7 October 2012, keeping a clean sheet in a 2–0 home victory. His appearance ended fellow Tottenham goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Brad_Friedel" title="Brad Friedel">Brad Friedel</a>'s run of 310 consecutive games in the Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> After conceding only four goals in six games, he was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for December 2012, but lost out to Manchester United's <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Lloris ended the 2012–13 season with 25 appearances and 9 clean sheets.
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14_season">2013–14 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2013–14 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following speculation linking him with a move to Monaco, Lloris insisted he had left Lyon to play abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> On 3 November 2013, in a match against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>, Lloris lost consciousness in a collision with <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a>'s knee, but remained in the game after manager <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Villas-Boas" title="André Villas-Boas">André Villas-Boas</a> determined he "showed great character and personality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeadInjury_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-HeadInjury-55">[55]</a></sup> The decision was heavily criticised by head injury charities, <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and the players' union, <a href="/wiki/FIFPro" title="FIFPro">FIFPro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HeadInjury_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-HeadInjury-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloris signed a five-year contract extension in July 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>  He said that <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a>, the new manager at Tottenham, had convinced him to sign the new contract with his "rigour and vision" that gave the club "new benchmarks".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15_season">2014–15 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2014–15 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Europa_League_group_stage" title="2014–15 UEFA Europa League group stage">2014–15 UEFA Europa League group stage</a> match on 23 October 2014, Tottenham were leading <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asteras_Tripolis_F.C." title="Asteras Tripolis F.C.">Asteras Tripoli</a> 5–0 with four minutes to play when Lloris was sent off for a professional foul on <a href="/wiki/Tasos_Tsokanis" title="Tasos Tsokanis">Tasos Tsokanis</a>. As the team had used all three substitutes, forward <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kane" title="Harry Kane">Harry Kane</a> was forced into goal and conceded a goal from a freekick in the 89th minute; Tottenham won the match 5–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asteras_Tripoli_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asteras_Tripoli-58">[58]</a></sup> Tottenham progressed through the League Cup to face Chelsea in the final at Wembley. Lloris was named in the starting eleven in the hopes of getting silverware but Tottenham lost 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015LeagueCupFinal_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015LeagueCupFinal-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season">2015–16 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2015–16 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In August 2015, Tottenham manager <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a> named Lloris permanent <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> of the team, replacing the outgoing <a href="/wiki/Youn%C3%A8s_Kaboul" title="Younès Kaboul">Younès Kaboul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season">2016–17 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2016–17 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League group stage">2016–17 UEFA Champions League group stage</a> match (which ended in a 0–0 draw) against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayer_Leverkusen" title="Bayer Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> on 18 October 2016, Lloris made a string of fine saves, including a spectacular one-handed stop on the goal-line to deny <a href="/wiki/Javier_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Javier Hernández">Javier Hernández</a>; Tottenham's manager <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a> described Lloris's performance in the second half as "brilliant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> On 22 November 2016, Lloris saved <a href="/wiki/Radamel_Falcao" title="Radamel Falcao">Radamel Falcao</a>'s 11th-minute penalty and pulled off multiple world-class saves, including incredibly tipping <a href="/wiki/Kamil_Glik" title="Kamil Glik">Kamil Glik</a>'s powerful volley from five metres out over the bar in the 68th minute, in their 2016–17 UEFA Champions League group stage match away at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AS_Monaco" title="AS Monaco">AS Monaco</a>; however Tottenham lost the match 1–2 and were eliminated from the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2016, Lloris signed a contract extension to remain at Tottenham until 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>  In the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">2016–17 season</a>, Lloris helped Tottenham achieve the best defensive record in the club's history, conceding only 26 goals in the Premier League this season (only 9 of which were conceded in home league games), 6 better than the previous record of 32 conceded that was set in the <a href="/wiki/1908%E2%80%9309_in_English_football" title="1908–09 in English football">1908–09 season</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> He kept 15 clean sheets this season, but missed out on the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Glove" title="Premier League Golden Glove">Golden Glove</a> award when a goal was conceded in the last game of the season, a record-breaking 7–1 away league win at <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season">2017–18 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2017–18 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 17 April 2018, Lloris made his 250th appearance for Tottenham in a 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton</a>. In doing so, he became only the 61st player, and sixth goalkeeper to achieve the milestone for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season">2018–19 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2018–19 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> group round match against <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> on 24 October 2018, Lloris was sent off after a challenge late in the game that ended in a 2–2 draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On 2 March 2019, Lloris saved a late penalty in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_London_Derby" title="North London Derby">North London Derby</a>, and kept the score at 1–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> A few days later on 5 March 2019, in the Champions League last-16 away tie against <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, Lloris made a number of crucial saves to kept a clean sheet, which ensured a 4–0 win on aggregate and progress to the club's second quarterfinal in the Champions League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> This is his 100th clean sheet with the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> He also kept a clean sheet in the home leg of the quarter-final against Manchester City, saving a penalty in a 1–0 win that helped keep Tottenham in the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The previous week in the Premier League match against Liverpool, he made a goalkeeping error which let in a late goal and lost 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season">2019–20 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2019–20 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2019–20 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2019–20 season</a>, Lloris made his 300th appearance for the club in second league match of the season against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>, a match that finished 2–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
On 5 October, Lloris was carried off on a stretcher after suffering a dislocated elbow against Brighton, a match which ended in 3-0 defeat for Spurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>  Ligament damage sustained in the injury would rule him out the team for a few months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In November 2019 he underwent surgery for the dislocation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="298" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg/160px-Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg/240px-Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hugo_Lloris_Euro_2012_v2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris playing for France at UEFA Euro 2012.</div></div></div>
<p>Lloris has been active on the international front with <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>, first appearing with the <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-18_football_team" title="France national under-18 football team">under-18 team</a> making his debut on 11 March 2004 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" title="Exhibition match">friendly match</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-18_football_team" title="Germany national under-18 football team">Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> He later played with the <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-19_football_team" title="France national under-19 football team">under-19 team</a> and was part of the winning team at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2005_European_Under-19_Football_Championship" title="2005 European Under-19 Football Championship">2005 European Under-19 Football Championship</a>. Lloris appeared in all five matches the team played in the competition. He made only five appearances with the <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-21_football_team" title="France national under-21 football team">under-21 team</a>, primarily because of his commitments to the senior team. On 11 October 2008, with the under-21 squad attempting to qualify for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_UEFA_European_Under-21_Football_Championship" title="2009 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship">2009 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship</a>, coach <a href="/wiki/Erick_Mombaerts" title="Erick Mombaerts">Erick Mombaerts</a> called up Lloris to the team for their important two-legged playoff against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-21_football_team" title="Germany national under-21 football team">Germany</a>, despite him having been called up to the senior team and the player having last played for the team in August 2007. Lloris honored the call up and started the second leg. With France seconds away from a spot in the tournament, because of the team's 1–1 draw in the first leg, Germany got a late goal from <a href="/wiki/Benedikt_H%C3%B6wedes" title="Benedikt Höwedes">Benedikt Höwedes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The 1–0 loss eliminated France from the competition and also ended Lloris's under-21 career.
</p><p>Lloris received his first call-up to the senior national team for France's 6 February 2008 match against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>. However, he instead played for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/France_B_national_football_team" title="France B national football team">the B team</a> in their friendly match against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_DR_national_football_team" title="Congo DR national football team">Congo DR</a>, held the day before the Spain friendly. After receiving several more call ups in 2008, he finally earned his first cap on 19 November 2008 in a 0–0 draw with <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a>. On 9 September 2009, Lloris received his first international <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card" title="Penalty card">red card</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_football_team" title="Serbia national football team">Serbia</a>, following a foul on <a href="/wiki/Nikola_%C5%BDigi%C4%87" title="Nikola Žigić">Nikola Žigić</a> in the penalty box, despite replays showing otherwise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Lloris returned to the team on 14 October playing the entire 90 minutes in the team's 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a>.
</p><p>Lloris was applauded by the media and players, alike, for his performance over two legs against the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> that saw France earn a spot in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> finals. Former national team goalkeeper Grégory Coupet credited his performance as "phenomenal", while the French media described him as "Saint Lloris", which is a play on the nickname of Real Madrid counterpart <a href="/wiki/Iker_Casillas" title="Iker Casillas">Iker Casillas</a>, who was considered one of the top goalkeepers in Europe at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 May 2010, Lloris was named in Domenech's 30-man preliminary squad to participate in the 2010 World Cup, later being named to the final 23-man team and installed as first-choice goalkeeper. On 11 June 2010, Lloris made his <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals debut in the team's opening group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a>, earning a clean sheet in a 0–0 draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Lloris appeared in both of France's other group stage matches, against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> and hosts <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a>. Against South Africa, Lloris committed a goalkeeping error which resulted in the opening goal for the hosts. He redeemed himself later in the match, however, by producing several saves to limit the South Africans' chances of progressing to the knockout rounds. France lost the match 2–1, which resulted in the hosts' elimination from the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="656" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg/240px-Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg/360px-Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg/480px-Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lloris_Torres_and_Koscielny_Sweden-France_Euro_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris (left) saves a shot from <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:France_WC2018_final.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1160" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/France_WC2018_final.jpg/240px-France_WC2018_final.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/France_WC2018_final.jpg/360px-France_WC2018_final.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/France_WC2018_final.jpg/480px-France_WC2018_final.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:France_WC2018_final.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lloris (top right), lining up with France during the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Final">2018 FIFA World Cup Final</a>.</div></div></div> 
<p>On 17 November 2010, Lloris <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captained</a> France, for the first time, in the team's 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> After leading France out six more times on an interim basis, on 28 February 2012, he was named first-choice captain of the national team by manager <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Blanc" title="Laurent Blanc">Laurent Blanc</a> ahead of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>. Lloris started for his country in the final tournament, as they reached the quarter-finals, where they were eliminated following a 2–0 loss to eventual champions Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p>He started for France at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 World Cup</a>, helping the team to the quarter-finals, where they were defeated 1–0 by eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lloris was the starting goalkeeper of the French squad that reached the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_Final" title="UEFA Euro 2016 Final">final</a> of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> on home soil, only to be defeated 1–0 by <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> in extra time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 June 2017, Lloris made his 88th appearance for France in a 5–0 friendly home win over <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a>, overtaking <a href="/wiki/Fabien_Barthez" title="Fabien Barthez">Fabien Barthez</a> as his nation's most capped goalkeeper of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> After beating <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belarus_national_football_team" title="Belarus national football team">Belarus</a> in October later that year, Hugo Lloris and the France national team <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">qualified</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 June 2018, Lloris earned his 100th cap in France's 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Peru_national_football_team" title="Peru national football team">Peru</a> in their second group stage game of the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Against Uruguay in the quarter-finals, Lloris made a key save from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Caceres" title="Martin Caceres">Martin Caceres</a> header as France won 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
On 15 July, he lifted the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Trophy" title="FIFA World Cup Trophy">World Cup trophy</a> as his team's captain, as France defeated <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> with a 4–2 victory in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2018_World_Cup_Final" title="2018 World Cup Final">final</a>, despite his mistake which allowed Croatia's <a href="/wiki/Mario_Mand%C5%BEuki%C4%87" title="Mario Mandžukić">Mario Mandžukić</a> to score a goal as Lloris tried to dribble past him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 November 2018, he made a record of 9 saves in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League" title="UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> game against <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a>, which France lost 0–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_style">Playing style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Playing style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lloris is described as a goalkeeper who "boasts lightning reflexes and good decision-making" and is "a formidable opponent in one-on-one situations". Lloris also "commands his box well".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> His playing style, and in particular his speed when coming off his line to anticipate opponents and clear the ball, has led him to be described as a <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)#Sweeper-keeper" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">sweeper-keeper</a> in the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> 
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lloris met Marine while he was studying at the Lycée Thierry Maulnier in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> On 23 September 2010, he announced the birth of their daughter, Anna-Rose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> They married at the Église Saint-François-de-Paule in <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a> in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Another daughter Giuliana was born in 2014 just before the World Cup in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heavy_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-heavy-104">[104]</a></sup> Their son Léandro was born on 20 September 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, while Lloris was playing for Nice, his mother died. Just two days after her death, he gained national respect for his refusal of a <a href="/wiki/Grief" title="Grief">bereavement</a> leave offer from manager <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Antonetti" title="Frédéric Antonetti">Frédéric Antonetti</a>, instead opting to play in a league match for Nice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 August 2010, Lloris was named, alongside international teammate <a href="/wiki/Karim_Benzema" title="Karim Benzema">Karim Benzema</a>, to appear on the cover of the French version of <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_11" title="FIFA 11">FIFA 11</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 August 2018, Lloris was charged with <a href="/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence" title="Driving under the influence">drink-driving</a> after being stopped by police in west London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Lloris later pleaded guilty at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Magistrates%27_Court" title="Westminster Magistrates' Court">Westminster Magistrates' Court</a> and admitted to being more than twice the drink-drive limit. He was fined £50,000 and banned from driving for 20 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hugo_Lloris&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><i>As of match played 7 September 2019</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloris,_Hugo_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lloris,_Hugo-110">[110]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">
<caption>Appearances and goals by national team and year
